\t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans\"\n12: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/providers\"\n13: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states\"\n14: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/tfdiags\"\n15: )\n16: \n17: // ApplyGraphBuilder implements GraphBuilder and is responsible for building\n18: // a graph for applying a Terraform diff.\n19: //\n20: // Because the graph is built from the diff (vs. the config or state),\n21: // this helps ensure that the apply-time graph doesn't modify any resources\n22: // that aren't explicitly in the diff. There are other scenarios where the\n23: // diff can be deviated, so this is just one layer of protection.\n24: type ApplyGraphBuilder struct {\n25: \t// Config is the configuration tree that the diff was built from.\n26: \tConfig *configs.Config\n27: \n28: \t// Changes describes the changes that we need apply.\n29: \tChanges *plans.Changes\n30: \n31: \t// DeferredChanges describes the changes that were deferred during the plan\n32: \t// and should not be applied.\n33: \tDeferredChanges []*plans.DeferredResourceInstanceChangeSrc\n34: \n35: \t// State is the current state\n36: \tState *states.State\n37: \n38: \t// RootVariableValues are the root module input variables captured as\n39: \t// part of the plan object, which we must reproduce in the apply step\n40: \t// to get a consistent result.\n41: \tRootVariableValues InputValues\n42: \n43: \t// ExternalProviderConfigs are pre-initialized root module provider\n44: \t// configurations that the graph builder should assume will be available\n45: \t// immediately during the subsequent plan walk, without any explicit\n46: \t// initialization step.\n47: \tExternalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n48: \n49: \t// Plugins is a library of the plug-in components (providers and\n50: \t// provisioners) available for use.\n51: \tPlugins *contextPlugins\n52: \n53: \t// Targets are resources to target. This is only required to make sure\n54: \t// unnecessary outputs aren't included in the apply graph. The plan\n55: \t// builder successfully handles targeting resources. In the future,\n56: \t// outputs should go into the diff so that this is unnecessary.\n57: \tTargets []addrs.Targetable\n58: \n59: \t// ForceReplace are the resource instance addresses that the user\n60: \t// requested to force replacement for when creating the plan, if any.\n61: \t// The apply step refers to these as part of verifying that the planned\n62: \t// actions remain consistent between plan and apply.\n63: \tForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n64: \n65: \t// Plan Operation this graph will be used for.\n66: \tOperation walkOperation\n67: \n68: \t// ExternalReferences allows the external caller to pass in references to\n69: \t// nodes that should not be pruned even if they are not referenced within\n70: \t// the actual graph.\n71: \tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\n72: \n73: \t// Overrides provides the set of overrides supplied by the testing\n74: \t// framework.\n75: \tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\n76: }\n77: \n78: // See GraphBuilder\n79: func (b *ApplyGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n80: \treturn (&BasicGraphBuilder{\n81: \t\tSteps: b.Steps(),\n82: \t\tName:  \"ApplyGraphBuilder\",\n83: \t}).Build(path)\n84: }\n85: \n86: // See GraphBuilder\n87: func (b *ApplyGraphBuilder) Steps() []GraphTransformer {\n88: \t// Custom factory for creating providers.\n89: \tconcreteProvider := func(a *NodeAbstractProvider) dag.Vertex {\n90: \t\treturn &NodeApplyableProvider{\n91: \t\t\tNodeAbstractProvider: a,\n92: \t\t}\n93: \t}\n94: \n95: \tconcreteResource := func(a *NodeAbstractResource) dag.Vertex {\n96: \t\treturn &nodeExpandApplyableResource{\n97: \t\t\tNodeAbstractResource: a,\n98: \t\t}\n99: \t}\n100: \n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/terraform--7637a921@44e4f8eb7b3616ffb2756cb26fb52bf3dd5534eb/-/blob/internal/terraform/graph_builder_apply.go%3FL1-100"}}}

Most callers should _not_\\n22: // explicitly lock, and should instead use the other methods of this type that\\n23: // handle locking automatically.\\n24: //\\n25: // Since SyncState is able to safely consolidate multiple updates into a single\\n26: // atomic operation, many of its methods are at a higher level than those\\n27: // of the underlying types, and operate on the state as a whole rather than\\n28: // on individual sub-structures of the state.\\n29: //\\n30: // SyncState can only protect against races within its own methods. It cannot\\n31: // provide any guarantees about the order in which concurrent operations will\\n32: // be processed, so callers may still need to employ higher-level techniques\\n33: // for ensuring correct operation sequencing, such as building and walking\\n34: // a dependency graph.\\n35: type SyncState struct {\\n36: \\tstate    *State\\n37: \\twritable bool\\n38: \\tlock     sync.RWMutex\\n39: }\\n40: \\n41: // Module returns a snapshot of the state of the module instance with the given\\n42: // address, or nil if no such module is tracked.\\n43: //\\n44: // The return value is a pointer to a copy of the module state, which the\\n45: // caller may then freely access and mutate. \\t\\\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs\\\"\\n11: \\t\\\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/checks\\\"\\n12: \\t\\\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty\\\"\\n13: )\\n14: \\n15: // SyncState is a wrapper around State that provides concurrency-safe access to\\n16: // various common operations that occur during a Terraform graph walk, or other\\n17: // similar concurrent contexts.\\n18: //\\n19: // When a SyncState wrapper is in use, no concurrent direct access to the\\n20: // underlying objects is permitted unless the caller first acquires an explicit\\n21: // lock, using the Lock and Unlock methods. Most callers should _not_\\n22: // explicitly lock, and should instead use the other methods of this type that\\n23: // handle locking automatically.\\n24: //\\n25: // Since SyncState is able to safely consolidate multiple updates into a single\\n26: // atomic operation, many of its methods are at a higher level than those\\n27: // of the underlying types, and operate on the state as a whole rather than\\n28: // on individual sub-structures of the state.\\n29: //\\n30: // SyncState can only protect against races within its own methods. It cannot\\n31: // provide any guarantees about the order in which concurrent operations will\\n32: // be processed, so callers may still need to employ higher-level techniques\\n33: // for ensuring correct operation sequencing, such as building and walking\\n34: // a dependency graph.\\n35: type SyncState struct {\\n36: \\tstate    *State\\n37: \\twritable bool\\n38: \\tlock     sync.RWMutex\\n39: }\\n40: \\n41: // Module returns a snapshot of the state of the module instance with the given\\n42: // address, or nil if no such module is tracked.\\n43: //\\n44: // The return value is a pointer to a copy of the module state, which the\\n45: // caller may then freely access and mutate. However, since the module state\\n46: // tends to be a large data structure with many child objects, where possible\\n47: // callers should prefer to use a more granular accessor to access a child\\n48: // module directly, and thus reduce the amount of copying required.\\n49: func (s *SyncState) Module(addr addrs.ModuleInstance) *Module {\\n50: \\ts.lock.RLock()\\n51: \\tret := s.state.Module(addr).DeepCopy()\\n52: \\ts.lock.RUnlock()\\n53: \\treturn ret\\n54: }\\n55: \\n56: // RemoveModule removes the entire state for the given module, taking with\\n57: // it any resources associated with the module. This should generally be\\n58: // called only for modules whose resources have all been destroyed, but\\n59: // that is not enforced by this method.\\n60: func (s *SyncState) RemoveModule(addr addrs.ModuleInstance) {\\n61: \\tdefer s.beginWrite()()\\n62: \\n63: \\ts.state.RemoveModule(addr)\\n64: }\\n65: \\n66: // OutputValue returns a snapshot of the state of the output value with the\\n67: // given address, or nil if no such output value is tracked.\\n68: //\\n69: // The return value is a pointer to a copy of the output value state, which the\\n70: // caller may then freely access and mutate.\\n71: func (s *SyncState) OutputValue(addr addrs.AbsOutputValue) *OutputValue {\\n72: \\ts.lock.RLock()\\n73: \\tret := s.state.OutputValue(addr).DeepCopy()\\n74: \\ts.lock.RUnlock()\\n75: \\treturn ret\\n76: }\\n77: \\n78: // SetOutputValue writes a given output value into the state, overwriting\\n79: // any existing value of the same name.\\n80: //\\n81: // The state only tracks output values for the root module, so attempts to\\n82: // write output values for any other module will be silently ignored.\\n83: func (s *SyncState) SetOutputValue(addr addrs.AbsOutputValue, value cty.Value, sensitive bool) {\\n84: \\tif !addr.Module.IsRoot() {\\n85: \\t\\treturn\\n86: \\t}\\n87: \\n88: \\tdefer s.beginWrite()()\\n89: \\ts.state.SetOutputValue(addr, caller may then freely access and mutate.\\n111: func (s *SyncState) Resource(addr addrs.AbsResource) *Resource {\\n112: \\ts.lock.RLock()\\n113: \\tret := s.state.Resource(addr).DeepCopy()\\n114: \\ts.lock.RUnlock()\\n115: \\treturn ret\\n116: }\\n117: \\n118: // ResourceInstance returns a snapshot of the state the resource instance with\\n119: // the given address, or nil if no such instance ret\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: // ResourceInstanceObject returns a snapshot of the resource instance object\\n131: // of the given deposed key belonging to the given resource instance. For example, this method is useful if reloading objects\\n231: // that were persisted to a state file. To mark the current object as deposed,\\n232: // use DeposeResourceInstanceObject instead.\\n233: //\\n234: // The caller must ensure that the given ResourceInstanceObject is not\\n235: // concurrently mutated during this call, but may be freely used again once\\n236: // this function returns.\\n237: //\\n238: // The resource that contains the given instance must already exist in the\\n239: // state, or this method will panic. // Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.\n2: // SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1\n3: \n4: package states\n5: \n6: import (\n7: \t\"log\"\n8: \t\"sync\"\n9: \n10: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs\"\n11: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/checks\"\n12: \t\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty\"\n13: )\n14: \n15: // SyncState is a wrapper around State that provides concurrency-safe access to\n16: // various common operations that occur during a Terraform graph walk, or other\n17: // similar concurrent contexts.\n18: //\n19: // When a SyncState wrapper is in use, no concurrent direct access to the\n20: // underlying objects is permitted unless the caller first acquires an explicit\n21: // lock, using the Lock and Unlock methods. Most callers should _not_\n22: // explicitly lock, and should instead use the other methods of this type that\n23: // handle locking automatically.\n24: //\n25: // Since SyncState is able to safely consolidate multiple updates into a single\n26: // atomic operation, many of its methods are at a higher level than those\n27: // of the underlying types, and operate on the state as a whole rather than\n28: // on individual sub-structures of the state.\n29: //\n30: // SyncState can only protect against races within its own methods. It cannot\n31: // provide any guarantees about the order in which concurrent operations will\n32: // be processed, so callers may still need to employ higher-level techniques\n33: // for ensuring correct operation sequencing, such as building and walking\n34: // a dependency graph.\n35: type SyncState struct {\n36: \tstate    *State\n37: \twritable bool\n38: \tlock     sync.RWMutex\n39: }\n40: \n41: // Module returns a snapshot of the state of the module instance with the given\n42: // address, or nil if no such module is tracked.\n43: //\n44: // The return value is a pointer to a copy of the module state, which the\n45: // caller may then freely access and mutate. However, since the module state\n46: // tends to be a large data structure with many child objects, where possible\n47: // callers should prefer to use a more granular accessor to access a child\n48: // module directly, and thus reduce the amount of copying required.\n49: func (s *SyncState) Module(addr addrs.ModuleInstance) *Module {\n50: \ts.lock.RLock()\n51: \tret := s.state.Module(addr).DeepCopy()\n52: \ts.lock.RUnlock()\n53: \treturn ret\n54: }\n55: \n56: // RemoveModule removes the entire state for the given module, taking with\n57: // it any resources associated with the module. This should generally be\n58: // called only for modules whose resources have all been destroyed, but\n59: // that is not enforced by this method.\n60: func (s *SyncState) RemoveModule(addr addrs.ModuleInstance) {\n61: \tdefer s.beginWrite()()\n62: \n63: \ts.state.RemoveModule(addr)\n64: }\n65: \n66: // OutputValue returns a snapshot of the state of the output value with the\n67: // given address, or nil if no such output value is tracked.\n68: //\n69: // The return value is a pointer to a copy of the output value state, which the\n70: // caller may then freely access and mutate.\n71: func (s *SyncState) OutputValue(addr addrs.AbsOutputValue) *OutputValue {\n72: \ts.lock.RLock()\n73: \tret := s.state.OutputValue(addr).DeepCopy()\n74: \ts.lock.RUnlock()\n75: \treturn ret\n76: }\n77: \n78: // SetOutputValue writes a given output value into the state, overwriting\n79: // any existing value of the same name.\n80: //\n81: // The state only tracks output values for the root module, so attempts to\n82: // write output values for any other module will be silently ignored.\n83: func (s *SyncState) SetOutputValue(addr addrs.AbsOutputValue, value cty.Value, sensitive
