{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01AsTktHSSrumXiwQEtg29y6","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01VTLsnm4Xan8oBSvFnaKmqR","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform's plan and apply operations are executed through a sophisticated graph-based execution engine. The architecture decomposes these operations into two major phases:\n\n1. **Graph Construction Phase**: Builds a directed acyclic graph (DAG) representing resources, their configurations, and their dependencies\n2. **Graph Execution Phase**: Traverses the graph respecting dependencies, executing operations in parallel where possible\n\nThis document details the internal architecture of these components and their interactions.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### 1.1 Core Graph Structure\n\nThe `Graph` type represents the execution plan as a directed acyclic graph with the following structure:\n\n```\nGraph\n├── dag.AcyclicGraph (embedded)\n└── Path: addrs.ModuleInstance  // Module scope for this graph\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains graph vertices (nodes) and edges (dependencies)\n- Validates that the graph is acyclic and has a single root\n- Provides traversal capabilities via the embedded `AcyclicGraph`\n- Supports concurrent graph walks through the `Walk()` method\n\n### 1.2 GraphBuilder Interface\n\nThe `GraphBuilder` interface defines how graphs are constructed:\n\n```go\ntype GraphBuilder interface {\n    Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n}\n```\n\nThe standard implementation is `BasicGraphBuilder`, which:\n- Maintains an ordered list of `GraphTransformer` steps\n- Executes each transformer in sequence, modifying the graph incrementally\n- Validates the final graph for cycles and connectivity\n- Logs graph state changes after each transformation step\n\n**Execution Pattern:**\n```\nGraphBuilder.Build()\n├── Create empty Graph\n├── For each GraphTransformer in Steps:\n│   ├── Call Transform(graph)\n│   ├── Log graph state\n│   └── Handle errors\n└── Validate graph (single root, no cycles)\n```\n\n### 1.3 Phase-Specific Graph Builders\n\n#### PlanGraphBuilder\n\nConstructs the execution graph for plan operations. Key characteristics:\n\n- **Source of Truth**: Configuration (desired state) combined with current state\n- **Decisions Based On**: Diff between prior state and configuration\n- **Does NOT Consider**: Lifecycle preferences like `create_before_destroy` (these are post-plan concerns)\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `Config`: Configuration tree representing desired state\n- `State`: Current state\n- `RootVariableValues`: Input variables provided by user\n- `Targets`: Resource targeting filters\n- `ForceReplace`: Resources to force replacement\n- `Plugins`: Provider and provisioner factory references\n\n#### ApplyGraphBuilder\n\nConstructs the execution graph for apply operations. Key characteristics:\n\n- **Source of Truth**: The Plan object (list of changes)\n- **Protects Against**: Applying resources not explicitly in the plan\n- **Decisions Based On**: The calculated changes from planning\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `Config`: Configuration (must match the plan's source config)\n- `Changes`: The plan changes to apply\n- `State`: Current state before applying changes\n- `Targets`: Resource targeting filters (for consistency checking)\n\n### 1.4 Graph Transformers\n\nGraph transformers implement the `GraphTransformer` interface:\n\n```go\ntype GraphTransformer interface {\n    Transform(*Graph) error\n}\n```\n\nTransformers incrementally build the execution graph by:\n1. **Adding nodes**: Creating graph vertices representing resources, providers, modules, etc.\n2. **Creating edges**: Establishing dependency relationships\n3. **Filtering**: Removing nodes that shouldn't be executed\n4. **Expanding**: Converting abstract nodes to concrete operational nodes\n\n#### Key Transformer Categories\n\n**Configuration Transformers:**\n- `ConfigTransformer`: Adds all resources from configuration to graph\n- `AttachConfigProviderTransformer`: Attaches provider configuration to nodes\n- `AttachConfigResourceTransformer`: Attaches resource configuration to resource nodes\n- `AttachSchemaTransformer`: Adds provider schemas for validation\n\n**State Transformers:**\n- `AttachStateTransformer`: Attaches prior state to resource nodes\n- `StateTransformer`: Adds state-only resources not in configuration (for cleanup)\n\n**Expansion Transformers:**\n- `ExpandTransformer`: Expands `count` and `for_each` resources into concrete instances\n- `ModuleExpansionTransformer`: Expands module calls into concrete module instances\n- These are critical for dynamic expansion during execution\n\n**Dependency Transformers:**\n- `ReferenceTransformer`: Builds edges based on resource references in expressions\n- `ProviderTransformer`: Adds provider nodes and establishes provider dependencies\n- `DestroyEdgeTransformer`: Creates special edges for resource destruction order\n- `DestroyCreateBeforeDestroyTransformer`: Implements lifecycle rules\n\n**Filtering Transformers:**\n- `TargetsTransformer`: Filters graph to only targeted resources and their dependencies\n- `OrphanTransformer`: Marks resources for destruction if removed from configuration\n- `TransitiveReductionTransformer`: Removes redundant edges to simplify execution\n\n**Ordering Transformers:**\n- `ImportStateTransformer`: Adds import operations\n- `CheckTransformer`: Adds check validation nodes\n- `VariableValidationTransformer`: Adds variable validation nodes\n\n### 1.5 Node Types and Abstraction\n\n#### Abstract Nodes\n\nAbstract nodes are transitional node types that represent the logical concept of an operation without being executable:\n\n- `NodeAbstractResource`: Base for resource-level operations\n- `NodeAbstractResourceInstance`: Base for single resource instance operations\n- `NodeAbstractProvider`: Base for provider operations\n- `NodeAbstractModule`: Base for module operations\n\n**Concrete Node Conversion:**\n\nThe graph builder uses factory functions to convert abstract nodes to concrete, executable types:\n\n```go\n// Factory function signature\ntype ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc func(*NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex\n\n// Usage in builders\nconcreteResourceInstance := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodeApplyableResourceInstance{\n        NodeAbstractResourceInstance: a,\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis allows the same abstract representation to be converted to different executable nodes depending on the operation (plan vs apply).\n\n#### Concrete Node Examples\n\n- `NodeApplyableResource`: Expansion node for apply phase\n- `NodePlanResourceInstance`: Plans changes for a resource instance\n- `NodeApplyableResourceInstance`: Applies a change to a resource instance\n- `NodeDestroyResourceInstance`: Destroys a resource instance\n- `NodeRefreshResourceInstance`: Refreshes a resource instance's state\n- `NodeApplyableProvider`: Initializes and configures a provider\n- `NodeDataSource`: Reads a data source\n- `NodeOutput`: Computes output values\n\n---\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### 2.1 Provider Initialization and Management\n\nProviders are lazily initialized during graph execution through the `EvalContext` interface.\n\n#### Initialization Sequence\n\n```\n1. Provider node execution begins\n2. EvalContext.InitProvider(addr, config) called\n3. Provider plugin loaded and instantiated\n4. Provider schema retrieved from plugin\n5. Provider stored in cache for reuse\n6. Subsequent references use cached provider\n```\n\n#### Key EvalContext Methods for Providers\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Initialize a provider with configuration\n    InitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider)\n        (providers.Interface, error)\n\n    // Retrieve already-initialized provider\n    Provider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) providers.Interface\n\n    // Get provider schema (must already be initialized)\n    ProviderSchema(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) (providers.ProviderSchema, error)\n\n    // Close provider connections when done\n    CloseProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) error\n\n    // Configure provider with merged config\n    ConfigureProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n### 2.2 Provider Configuration and Input\n\nProvider configuration is built by merging multiple sources:\n\n```\nProvider Configuration = User Input + Explicit Config + Parent Config\n```\n\n**Priority Order:**\n1. User input from interactive prompts (highest priority)\n2. Explicit configuration from HCL\n3. Parent provider configuration (for child modules)\n\nThe `buildProviderConfig()` function handles this merging:\n\n```go\nfunc buildProviderConfig(ctx EvalContext, addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig,\n    config *configs.Provider) hcl.Body {\n    // Merge input and explicit config\n    // User input takes priority\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 Provider Plugin Architecture\n\nProviders are external plugins communicating via gRPC. The plugin lifecycle:\n\n1. **Discovery**: Providers found in `.terraform/plugins` or installed via provider requirements\n2. **Loading**: Plugin binary launched as subprocess\n3. **Handshake**: Protocol negotiation and capability discovery\n4. **Schema Fetch**: Request provider schema definition\n5. **Configuration**: Provider receives merged configuration\n6. **Resource Operations**: Provider executes Create/Read/Update/Delete operations\n7. **Cleanup**: Provider process terminates when `CloseProvider()` called\n\n### 2.4 Resource Operation Delegation\n\nWhen a resource operation is planned or applied:\n\n```\nNode.Execute()\n├── Get provider from EvalContext\n├── Request resource schema from provider\n├── Build request object (state + config)\n├── Call provider method (PlanResourceChange, ApplyResourceChange, etc.)\n├── Capture response (planned/new state, error)\n└── Update local state with response\n```\n\nEach provider method is responsible for:\n- Validating arguments\n- Computing differences (for Plan)\n- Making API calls\n- Handling errors\n- Returning updated resource state\n\n---\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### 3.1 State Structure\n\nThe `State` type represents Terraform's persistent state:\n\n```\nState\n├── Modules: map[string]*Module\n│   └── Module (for each module instance)\n│       ├── Resources: map[string]*Resource\n│       │   └── Resource\n│       │       └── Instances: map[addrs.InstanceKey]*ResourceInstance\n│       │           └── ResourceInstance\n│       │               ├── Current: *ResourceInstanceObject\n│       │               └── Deposed: map[DeposedKey]*ResourceInstanceObject\n│       └── Outputs: map[string]*OutputValue\n├── RootOutputValues: map[string]*OutputValue\n└── CheckResults: *CheckResults\n```\n\n**Key Properties:**\n- **Hierarchical**: Organized by modules and resources\n- **Instance-Based**: Resources can have multiple instances (count/for_each)\n- **Deposed Objects**: Tracks old objects during create-before-destroy operations\n- **Immutable Interface**: State should only be modified through `SyncState` methods\n\n### 3.2 State Synchronization (SyncState)\n\nFor concurrent graph execution, state is wrapped in `SyncState`:\n\n```go\ntype SyncState struct {\n    state    *State\n    writable bool\n    lock     sync.RWMutex  // Protects concurrent access\n}\n```\n\n**Features:**\n- Atomic operations: Multiple state changes happen together or not at all\n- Read-Write separation: Multiple readers or single writer\n- Deep copying: Returned values are independent copies\n- Automatic pruning: Empty modules are removed (except root)\n\n**High-Level Operations:**\n\n```go\n// Resource instance operations\nSetResourceInstanceCurrent(addr, obj, provider)\nDeposeResourceInstanceObject(addr) DeposedKey\nSetResourceInstanceDeposed(addr, key, obj, provider)\n\n// Output operations\nSetOutputValue(addr, value, sensitive)\nRemoveOutputValue(addr)\n\n// Module operations\nRemoveModule(addr)\n\n// Batch operations for planning\nUpdateResourceInstanceObjects(...)\n```\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Enables concurrent graph node execution without race conditions\n- Provides consistent snapshots for reading\n- Prevents partial state updates during failures\n\n### 3.3 Multiple State Versions During Execution\n\nTerraform maintains multiple state objects simultaneously during a walk:\n\n```\nState: Current state being built\n    ↑\n    └── Updated by Apply/Plan nodes\n\nRefreshState: State after refresh phase\n    ↑\n    └── Populated during refresh walk\n\nPrevRunState: State from previous run\n    ↑\n    └── Loaded at start, used for comparison\n```\n\n**Usage:**\n- `State`: Primary state being modified\n- `RefreshState`: Previous state snapshot (for change detection)\n- `PrevRunState`: Used for comparisons and understanding drift\n\nThis enables:\n- Change detection: Compare current vs previous state\n- Rollback capability: Previous state preserved\n- Consistency checking: Ensure applied changes match plan\n\n### 3.4 State Persistence and Backends\n\nState management is abstracted through the state manager interface in `statemgr` package:\n\n```\nBackend (e.g., S3, Azure Storage)\n    ↑\nState Manager (implements locking, versioning)\n    ↑\nLocal State File (JSON format)\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- **Reading**: Load state from backend\n- **Locking**: Prevent concurrent operations\n- **Versioning**: Track state history\n- **Persistence**: Write updated state back to backend\n\nThe Context holds a reference to the state manager for:\n- Initial state loading\n- Atomic write-back after successful apply\n- Lock management during operations\n\n---\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Hook System\n\n### 4.1 Overall Plan Execution Flow\n\n```\nContext.Plan(config, opts)\n│\n├─ 1. Build Plan Graph\n│   ├── PlanGraphBuilder.Build()\n│   ├── Apply transformers in sequence\n│   └── Return executable Graph\n│\n├─ 2. Refresh Walk (optional)\n│   ├── Walk graph with RefreshWalker\n│   ├── Call resource ReadState for current values\n│   ├── Update RefreshState with current values\n│   └── Returns refreshed state for comparison\n│\n├─ 3. Plan Walk\n│   ├── Walk graph with PlanWalker\n│   ├── For each resource node:\n│   │   ├── Call provider.PlanResourceChange()\n│   │   ├── Capture planned change (Create/Update/Delete/NoOp)\n│   │   └── Store in Changes\n│   └── Returns complete change set\n│\n└─ 4. Return Plan Object\n    └── Contains all changes ready for apply\n```\n\n### 4.2 Overall Apply Execution Flow\n\n```\nContext.Apply(plan, config, opts)\n│\n├─ 1. Build Apply Graph\n│   ├── ApplyGraphBuilder.Build(plan.Changes)\n│   ├── Only includes changed resources\n│   ├── Applies create-before-destroy ordering\n│   └── Return executable Graph\n│\n├─ 2. Apply Walk\n│   ├── Walk graph with ApplyWalker\n│   ├── For each resource change node:\n│   │   ├── Call provider resource operation (Create/Update/Delete)\n│   │   ├── Update state with result\n│   │   └── Call hooks (PreApply, PostApply)\n│   ├── Handle deposed objects cleanup\n│   └── Update State atomically\n│\n└─ 3. Return Updated State\n    └── State persisted to backend\n```\n\n### 4.3 Graph Traversal (Walker)\n\nThe DAG walker executes nodes respecting dependencies:\n\n```\nWalker Algorithm:\n│\n├─ For each vertex (node) in graph:\n│   ├── Wait for all dependencies to complete\n│   ├── If dependency failed: Skip or error (per graph semantics)\n│   ├── Execute node callback (concurrent if possible)\n│   ├── Collect diagnostics\n│   └── Mark vertex complete\n│\n└─ Return aggregated diagnostics from all vertices\n```\n\n**Key Walker Characteristics:**\n- **Parallel Execution**: Independent nodes execute concurrently\n- **Dependency Respect**: Nodes only execute after upstream dependencies complete\n- **Atomic Failures**: Failed nodes block downstream dependents\n- **Cancelable**: Graph walk can be stopped via context cancellation\n\n### 4.4 Execution in ContextGraphWalker\n\nThe `ContextGraphWalker` implements the Terraform-specific walker pattern:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    Context              *Context\n    State                *states.SyncState    // Main state\n    RefreshState         *states.SyncState    // Pre-walk state snapshot\n    Changes              *plans.ChangesSync   // Accumulates changes\n    Checks               *checks.State\n    NamedValues          *namedvals.State     // Variable/output tracking\n    InstanceExpander     *instances.Expander  // Count/for_each expansion\n    Operation            walkOperation\n    StopContext          context.Context\n}\n\n// Key method called for each node\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) Execute(ctx EvalContext, node GraphNodeExecutable) {\n    // Acquire parallelism semaphore\n    w.Context.parallelSem.Acquire()\n    defer w.Context.parallelSem.Release()\n\n    // Execute the node\n    return node.Execute(ctx, w.Operation)\n}\n```\n\n**Scope Management:**\n\nThe walker maintains multiple evaluation contexts, one per module:\n\n```go\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) enterScope(scope evalContextScope) EvalContext {\n    // Returns EvalContext scoped to a specific module\n    // Caches contexts to ensure consistency\n}\n```\n\nThis allows:\n- Module isolation\n- Variable scope containment\n- Provider configuration inheritance\n\n### 4.5 Hook System\n\nHooks are callback points allowing external code to observe and influence execution.\n\n#### Hook Interface\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    // Resource operation hooks\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        newState cty.Value, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Plan hooks\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        priorState, proposedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Provisioning hooks\n    PreProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, err error) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, line string)\n\n    // State refresh hooks\n    PreRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, newState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Import hooks\n    PreImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, importID string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []providers.ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Lifecycle hooks\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error)\n    Stopping()\n}\n```\n\n#### Hook Actions\n\n```go\ntype HookAction byte\n\nconst (\n    HookActionContinue  // Proceed normally\n    HookActionHalt      // Cancel operation\n)\n```\n\n#### Hook Execution Flow\n\n```\nFor each hook in Context.hooks:\n    Call hook method with resource details\n    ├─ HookActionContinue: Proceed to next hook\n    └─ HookActionHalt: Cancel operation, stop remaining hooks\n```\n\n#### Common Hook Uses\n\n1. **UI Output**: Display resource operations and status\n2. **Logging**: Track operations for audit\n3. **Monitoring**: Integrate with external systems\n4. **Validation**: Custom checks during apply\n5. **Deferral**: Implement custom pause/resume logic\n\n### 4.6 Dynamic Expansion During Execution\n\nCount and for_each resources are expanded dynamically during graph execution.\n\n#### Instance Expansion\n\n```\nInstance Expander tracks:\n├─ count.index / each.key / each.value for current iteration\n├─ length calculations for count\n├─ map iterations for for_each\n└─ Nested expansion for resource instances\n```\n\n**Expansion Process:**\n\n```\n1. InstanceExpander node executes\n   ├── Evaluates count or for_each expression\n   └── Creates abstract instances for each value\n\n2. Instance keys created: IntKey for count, StringKey for for_each\n\n3. Per-instance nodes created from abstract node\n   ├── NodeResourcePlanInstance\n   ├── NodeResourceApplyInstance\n   └── Can access instance key for self references\n\n4. Instances execute in graph order\n   └── Each instance has independent state/attributes\n```\n\n**Data Available to Instances:**\n\n```\nself.*              // Current resource's computed attributes\ncount.index         // Numeric index (count)\neach.key            // Map key (for_each)\neach.value          // Map value (for_each)\nresource.*.id       // Splat referencing other instances\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Evaluation Context\n\n### 5.1 EvalContext Interface\n\nThe `EvalContext` is the primary interface for node execution, providing access to:\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Module and path information\n    Path() addrs.ModuleInstance\n    Stopped() <-chan struct{}\n\n    // Provider operations\n    InitProvider(addr, config) providers.Interface\n    Provider(addr) providers.Interface\n    ProviderSchema(addr) providers.ProviderSchema\n    CloseProvider(addr) error\n    ConfigureProvider(addr, config) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n    // Provisioners\n    Provisioner(name) provisioners.Interface\n    ProvisionerSchema(name) *configschema.Block\n\n    // State and changes\n    State() *states.SyncState\n    RefreshState() *states.SyncState\n    Changes() *plans.ChangesSync\n    NamedValues() *namedvals.State\n\n    // Expression evaluation\n    EvaluateBlock(body, schema, self, key) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluateExpr(expr, wantType, self) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluationScope(self, source, key) *lang.Scope\n\n    // Hooks and plugins\n    Hook(callback func(Hook) error) error\n    Input() UIInput\n}\n```\n\n### 5.2 BuiltinEvalContext Implementation\n\nThe standard implementation provides:\n\n```go\ntype BuiltinEvalContext struct {\n    // Execution environment\n    StopContext  context.Context\n    InstanceExpander *instances.Expander\n\n    // Caches\n    ProviderCache      map[string]providers.Interface\n    ProvisionerCache   map[string]provisioners.Interface\n\n    // State and configuration\n    StateValue         *states.SyncState\n    ChangesValue       *plans.ChangesSync\n    ChecksValue        *checks.State\n    NamedValuesValue   *namedvals.State\n    DeferralsValue     *deferring.Deferred\n\n    // Configuration\n    ConfigValue        *configs.Config\n    PluginsValue       *contextPlugins\n\n    // Evaluation\n    EvaluatorValue     *Evaluator\n}\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains caches for provider/provisioner instances\n- Coordinates access to state and changes\n- Provides expression evaluation capabilities\n- Manages hook invocation\n\n### 5.3 Evaluation and Expression Handling\n\nThe `Evaluator` handles HCL expression evaluation:\n\n```\nExpression Evaluation:\n│\n├─ Parse expression as HCL\n├─ Build evaluation scope with:\n│   ├── Module variables\n│   ├── Local values\n│   ├── Resource references\n│   ├── Data source references\n│   └── Functions and operators\n├─ Execute evaluation in scope\n├─ Apply type conversion if needed\n└─ Return evaluated cty.Value\n```\n\n**Scope Includes:**\n- `self.*`: Current resource or data source\n- Variables from root and current module\n- Outputs from all modules\n- Data source read values\n- Locals from current module\n- References to other resources/data sources\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points\n\n### 6.1 Custom Transformers\n\nExtend graph building by implementing `GraphTransformer`:\n\n```go\ntype CustomTransformer struct {\n    // Configuration\n}\n\nfunc (t *CustomTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {\n    // Add, remove, or modify nodes and edges\n    return nil\n}\n\n// Register with graph builder\nbuilder.Steps = append(builder.Steps, &CustomTransformer{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Custom node scheduling\n- Integration-specific resource ordering\n- Cost optimization by graph reordering\n- Security enforcement via forced dependencies\n\n### 6.2 Custom Hooks\n\nImplement `Hook` interface to observe execution:\n\n```go\ntype CustomHook struct{\n}\n\nfunc (h *CustomHook) PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, ...) (HookAction, error) {\n    // Log, validate, or modify behavior\n    return HookActionContinue, nil\n}\n\n// Register with context\nopts.Hooks = append(opts.Hooks, &CustomHook{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Real-time operation monitoring\n- Cost estimation\n- Resource validation\n- Event forwarding to external systems\n- Custom approval workflows\n\n### 6.3 Provider Plugins\n\nProviders are the primary extension point. Implement the `providers.Interface`:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetSchema(ctx context.Context) (*ProviderSchema, error)\n    PrepareProviderConfig(ctx context.Context, req PrepareProviderConfigRequest) PrepareProviderConfigResponse\n    ValidateResourceConfig(ctx context.Context, req ValidateResourceConfigRequest) ValidateResourceConfigResponse\n    ReadResource(ctx context.Context, req ReadResourceRequest) ReadResourceResponse\n    PlanResourceChange(ctx context.Context, req PlanResourceChangeRequest) PlanResourceChangeResponse\n    ApplyResourceChange(ctx context.Context, req ApplyResourceChangeRequest) ApplyResourceChangeResponse\n    // ... more methods\n}\n```\n\n**Hook Points:**\n- Configuration validation\n- Resource diffing\n- Resource creation, update, deletion\n- State refresh\n- Data source reads\n\n### 6.4 Custom Provisioners\n\nImplement `provisioners.Interface` for post-apply provisioning:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetSchema(ctx context.Context) (*configschema.Block, error)\n    ProvisionResource(ctx context.Context, req ProvisionResourceRequest) ProvisionResourceResponse\n    Stop(ctx context.Context) error\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Configuration management (Ansible, Chef, Puppet)\n- Custom deployment scripts\n- Infrastructure validation\n- Service registration\n\n---\n\n## 7. Error Handling\n\n### 7.1 Error Propagation\n\nErrors are collected and propagated through the execution flow:\n\n```\nNode.Execute() returns tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    ↓\nDiagnostic collected in walker\n    ↓\nWalker stops dependent nodes\n    ↓\nAggregated diagnostics returned to caller\n```\n\n**Diagnostic Types:**\n- `Error`: Prevents operation and downstream nodes\n- `Warning`: Logged but doesn't block execution\n- `Detail`: Informational messages\n\n### 7.2 Failure Handling in Parallel Execution\n\nWhen a node fails:\n\n1. **Downstream Blocking**: Dependent nodes receive error signal and don't execute\n2. **Parallel Sibling Isolation**: Independent nodes continue executing\n3. **Partial Completion**: Some resources may have executed before failure\n4. **State Preservation**: State partially updated with successful operations\n\n**Recovery Strategy:**\n- User can fix error and rerun plan/apply\n- Partial state is not persisted without full success\n- Deferred resources allow deferring problematic resources to next run\n\n### 7.3 Non-Fatal Errors\n\nSome errors don't block execution:\n\n```go\ntype NonFatalError interface {\n    Diagnostics() tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\nThese allow:\n- Collection of multiple issues\n- User fixing issues in one pass\n- Proceeding with partial results when appropriate\n\n---\n\n## 8. Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\n┌─────────────────┐\n│  Configuration  │\n│   (HCL files)   │\n└────────┬────────┘\n         │\n         v\n┌─────────────────────────┐\n│  Config Loader          │\n│  (parses, validates)    │\n└────────┬────────────────┘\n         │\n         v\n┌─────────────────────────┐\n│ Graph Builder           │\n│ (PlanGraphBuilder)      │\n├─────────────────────────┤\n│ Steps:                  │\n│ 1. ConfigTransformer    │\n│ 2. ExpandTransformer    │\n│ 3. ReferenceTransformer │\n│ 4. ProviderTransformer  │\n│ 5. ... (more)           │\n└────────┬────────────────┘\n         │\n         v\n    ┌─Graph─────┐\n    │ Nodes     │\n    │ (abstract)│\n    │ Edges     │\n    │ (deps)    │\n    └─────┬─────┘\n          │\n          v\n┌──────────────────────────────┐\n│ Concrete Node Conversion      │\n│ (factories apply)             │\n└──────────┬───────────────────┘\n           │\n           v\n     ┌─Graph────────┐\n     │ Executable   │\n     │ Nodes        │\n     │ (concrete)   │\n     │ Edges        │\n     └──────┬───────┘\n            │\n            v\n   ┌────────────────────┐\n   │ Refresh Walk       │ ← (optional)\n   ├────────────────────┤\n   │ ContextGraphWalker │\n   │ RefreshState       │\n   │ (ReadResource ops) │\n   └────────┬───────────┘\n            │\n            v\n   ┌────────────────────┐\n   │ Plan Walk          │\n   ├────────────────────┤\n   │ ContextGraphWalker │\n   │ Changes (build)    │\n   │ Hooks: Pre/Post*   │\n   └────────┬───────────┘\n            │\n            v\n    ┌───Plan Object───┐\n    │ Changes         │\n    │ ResourceChanges │\n    │ OutputChanges   │\n    └────────┬────────┘\n             │\n             v\n   ┌──────────────────────────┐\n   │ Graph Builder            │\n   │ (ApplyGraphBuilder)      │\n   │ (rebuilds from plan)     │\n   └───────────┬──────────────┘\n               │\n               v\n         ┌─Graph─────┐\n         │ Apply Ops │\n         └─────┬─────┘\n               │\n               v\n    ┌──────────────────────┐\n    │ Apply Walk           │\n    ├──────────────────────┤\n    │ ContextGraphWalker   │\n    │ State (update)       │\n    │ Hooks: Pre/Post*     │\n    │ Provider operations  │\n    └──────────┬───────────┘\n               │\n               v\n      ┌───Updated State────┐\n      │ Resources          │\n      │ (new attributes)   │\n      │ Outputs (computed) │\n      └────────┬───────────┘\n               │\n               v\n    ┌──────────────────┐\n    │ Backend Persist  │\n    │ (state file)     │\n    └──────────────────┘\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Performance Considerations\n\n### 9.1 Parallelism\n\nGraph execution naturally parallelizes:\n\n**Without Dependencies**: 100 independent resources execute concurrently (up to parallelism limit)\n\n**With Dependencies**: Resources execute in dependency order, but siblings execute in parallel\n\n```\nExample:\naws_vpc.main (Parallelism: 1/10)\n├─ aws_subnet.a (Parallelism: 2/10)\n├─ aws_subnet.b (Parallelism: 3/10)\n└─ aws_subnet.c (Parallelism: 4/10)\n   ├─ aws_instance.1 (Parallelism: 5/10)\n   ├─ aws_instance.2 (Parallelism: 6/10)\n   └─ aws_instance.3 (Parallelism: 7/10)\n```\n\n### 9.2 State Access Optimization\n\n`SyncState` minimizes lock contention:\n\n- Atomic operations reduce lock time\n- Deep copies prevent concurrent mutations\n- Module-level granularity allows targeting\n- Read-write separation maximizes parallelism\n\n### 9.3 Graph Construction Time\n\nLarge graphs (100s of resources) build in milliseconds:\n\n- Transformers run sequentially (single-threaded)\n- Most transformers run in O(n) or O(n log n)\n- TransitiveReduction can be expensive (O(VE)) but optional\n\n### 9.4 Execution Time Optimization Opportunities\n\n1. **Targeted apply**: Only resources with changes\n2. **Parallelism tuning**: `-parallelism=N` flag\n3. **Resource ordering**: Explicit `depends_on` for critical paths\n4. **Deferred actions**: Postpone problematic resources\n5. **Caching**: Provider schemas cached, reused across module instances\n\n---\n\n## 10. Key Architectural Patterns\n\n### 10.1 Builder Pattern\n\nThe `BasicGraphBuilder` + `GraphTransformer` chain:\n\n```\nEmpty Graph → Step 1 → Step 2 → ... → Step N → Final Graph\n```\n\nEach step is independent, composable, and testable.\n\n### 10.2 Visitor Pattern\n\n`GraphWalker` visits each node and executes it:\n\n```go\ntype GraphWalker interface {\n    Execute(EvalContext, GraphNodeExecutable)\n}\n```\n\nAllows flexible execution strategies (sequential, parallel, with caching, etc.)\n\n### 10.3 Strategy Pattern\n\nOperation-specific behavior through factories:\n\n```go\n// Plan operation\nconcretePlan := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodePlanResourceInstance{...}\n}\n\n// Apply operation\nconcreteApply := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodeApplyResourceInstance{...}\n}\n```\n\n### 10.4 Template Method Pattern\n\nAbstract nodes define the template, concrete nodes implement steps:\n\n```go\ntype NodeAbstractResourceInstance struct {\n    // Common attributes\n    Addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\n    // Implemented by concrete nodes\n    Execute() // Defined in NodePlanResourceInstance, etc.\n}\n```\n\n### 10.5 Observer Pattern\n\nHooks observe execution:\n\n```go\nHook interface {\n    PreApply(...)\n    PostApply(...)\n    // ... other observation points\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform's plan/apply architecture is built on these key principles:\n\n1. **Graph-Based Execution**: Dependencies drive parallelism\n2. **Phase Separation**: Planning and application are distinct phases\n3. **Plugin Architecture**: Providers implement resource operations\n4. **Thread-Safe State**: SyncState enables concurrent execution\n5. **Extensible Design**: Transformers and hooks allow customization\n6. **Composable Components**: Each piece is testable and replaceable\n7. **Error Isolation**: Failures don't corrupt state\n8. **Transparent Execution**: Hooks enable observation and control\n\nThis architecture enables Terraform to handle complex infrastructure as code scenarios with reliability, performance, and extensibility.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":7553,"cache_read_input_tokens":77860,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":7553},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"cbdb7d02-af08-4d38-80ab-7a2e3c902fb3","uuid":"0b93cc99-c212-4172-979b-e5faff33cbb9"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01VTLsnm4Xan8oBSvFnaKmqR","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/documentation.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"cbdb7d02-af08-4d38-80ab-7a2e3c902fb3","uuid":"d5c36e26-3137-4ff1-8b7d-7fa54ea2cb96","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform's plan and apply operations are executed through a sophisticated graph-based execution engine. The architecture decomposes these operations into two major phases:\n\n1. **Graph Construction Phase**: Builds a directed acyclic graph (DAG) representing resources, their configurations, and their dependencies\n2. **Graph Execution Phase**: Traverses the graph respecting dependencies, executing operations in parallel where possible\n\nThis document details the internal architecture of these components and their interactions.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### 1.1 Core Graph Structure\n\nThe `Graph` type represents the execution plan as a directed acyclic graph with the following structure:\n\n```\nGraph\n├── dag.AcyclicGraph (embedded)\n└── Path: addrs.ModuleInstance  // Module scope for this graph\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains graph vertices (nodes) and edges (dependencies)\n- Validates that the graph is acyclic and has a single root\n- Provides traversal capabilities via the embedded `AcyclicGraph`\n- Supports concurrent graph walks through the `Walk()` method\n\n### 1.2 GraphBuilder Interface\n\nThe `GraphBuilder` interface defines how graphs are constructed:\n\n```go\ntype GraphBuilder interface {\n    Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n}\n```\n\nThe standard implementation is `BasicGraphBuilder`, which:\n- Maintains an ordered list of `GraphTransformer` steps\n- Executes each transformer in sequence, modifying the graph incrementally\n- Validates the final graph for cycles and connectivity\n- Logs graph state changes after each transformation step\n\n**Execution Pattern:**\n```\nGraphBuilder.Build()\n├── Create empty Graph\n├── For each GraphTransformer in Steps:\n│   ├── Call Transform(graph)\n│   ├── Log graph state\n│   └── Handle errors\n└── Validate graph (single root, no cycles)\n```\n\n### 1.3 Phase-Specific Graph Builders\n\n#### PlanGraphBuilder\n\nConstructs the execution graph for plan operations. Key characteristics:\n\n- **Source of Truth**: Configuration (desired state) combined with current state\n- **Decisions Based On**: Diff between prior state and configuration\n- **Does NOT Consider**: Lifecycle preferences like `create_before_destroy` (these are post-plan concerns)\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `Config`: Configuration tree representing desired state\n- `State`: Current state\n- `RootVariableValues`: Input variables provided by user\n- `Targets`: Resource targeting filters\n- `ForceReplace`: Resources to force replacement\n- `Plugins`: Provider and provisioner factory references\n\n#### ApplyGraphBuilder\n\nConstructs the execution graph for apply operations. Key characteristics:\n\n- **Source of Truth**: The Plan object (list of changes)\n- **Protects Against**: Applying resources not explicitly in the plan\n- **Decisions Based On**: The calculated changes from planning\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `Config`: Configuration (must match the plan's source config)\n- `Changes`: The plan changes to apply\n- `State`: Current state before applying changes\n- `Targets`: Resource targeting filters (for consistency checking)\n\n### 1.4 Graph Transformers\n\nGraph transformers implement the `GraphTransformer` interface:\n\n```go\ntype GraphTransformer interface {\n    Transform(*Graph) error\n}\n```\n\nTransformers incrementally build the execution graph by:\n1. **Adding nodes**: Creating graph vertices representing resources, providers, modules, etc.\n2. **Creating edges**: Establishing dependency relationships\n3. **Filtering**: Removing nodes that shouldn't be executed\n4. **Expanding**: Converting abstract nodes to concrete operational nodes\n\n#### Key Transformer Categories\n\n**Configuration Transformers:**\n- `ConfigTransformer`: Adds all resources from configuration to graph\n- `AttachConfigProviderTransformer`: Attaches provider configuration to nodes\n- `AttachConfigResourceTransformer`: Attaches resource configuration to resource nodes\n- `AttachSchemaTransformer`: Adds provider schemas for validation\n\n**State Transformers:**\n- `AttachStateTransformer`: Attaches prior state to resource nodes\n- `StateTransformer`: Adds state-only resources not in configuration (for cleanup)\n\n**Expansion Transformers:**\n- `ExpandTransformer`: Expands `count` and `for_each` resources into concrete instances\n- `ModuleExpansionTransformer`: Expands module calls into concrete module instances\n- These are critical for dynamic expansion during execution\n\n**Dependency Transformers:**\n- `ReferenceTransformer`: Builds edges based on resource references in expressions\n- `ProviderTransformer`: Adds provider nodes and establishes provider dependencies\n- `DestroyEdgeTransformer`: Creates special edges for resource destruction order\n- `DestroyCreateBeforeDestroyTransformer`: Implements lifecycle rules\n\n**Filtering Transformers:**\n- `TargetsTransformer`: Filters graph to only targeted resources and their dependencies\n- `OrphanTransformer`: Marks resources for destruction if removed from configuration\n- `TransitiveReductionTransformer`: Removes redundant edges to simplify execution\n\n**Ordering Transformers:**\n- `ImportStateTransformer`: Adds import operations\n- `CheckTransformer`: Adds check validation nodes\n- `VariableValidationTransformer`: Adds variable validation nodes\n\n### 1.5 Node Types and Abstraction\n\n#### Abstract Nodes\n\nAbstract nodes are transitional node types that represent the logical concept of an operation without being executable:\n\n- `NodeAbstractResource`: Base for resource-level operations\n- `NodeAbstractResourceInstance`: Base for single resource instance operations\n- `NodeAbstractProvider`: Base for provider operations\n- `NodeAbstractModule`: Base for module operations\n\n**Concrete Node Conversion:**\n\nThe graph builder uses factory functions to convert abstract nodes to concrete, executable types:\n\n```go\n// Factory function signature\ntype ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc func(*NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex\n\n// Usage in builders\nconcreteResourceInstance := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodeApplyableResourceInstance{\n        NodeAbstractResourceInstance: a,\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis allows the same abstract representation to be converted to different executable nodes depending on the operation (plan vs apply).\n\n#### Concrete Node Examples\n\n- `NodeApplyableResource`: Expansion node for apply phase\n- `NodePlanResourceInstance`: Plans changes for a resource instance\n- `NodeApplyableResourceInstance`: Applies a change to a resource instance\n- `NodeDestroyResourceInstance`: Destroys a resource instance\n- `NodeRefreshResourceInstance`: Refreshes a resource instance's state\n- `NodeApplyableProvider`: Initializes and configures a provider\n- `NodeDataSource`: Reads a data source\n- `NodeOutput`: Computes output values\n\n---\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### 2.1 Provider Initialization and Management\n\nProviders are lazily initialized during graph execution through the `EvalContext` interface.\n\n#### Initialization Sequence\n\n```\n1. Provider node execution begins\n2. EvalContext.InitProvider(addr, config) called\n3. Provider plugin loaded and instantiated\n4. Provider schema retrieved from plugin\n5. Provider stored in cache for reuse\n6. Subsequent references use cached provider\n```\n\n#### Key EvalContext Methods for Providers\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Initialize a provider with configuration\n    InitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider)\n        (providers.Interface, error)\n\n    // Retrieve already-initialized provider\n    Provider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) providers.Interface\n\n    // Get provider schema (must already be initialized)\n    ProviderSchema(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) (providers.ProviderSchema, error)\n\n    // Close provider connections when done\n    CloseProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) error\n\n    // Configure provider with merged config\n    ConfigureProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n### 2.2 Provider Configuration and Input\n\nProvider configuration is built by merging multiple sources:\n\n```\nProvider Configuration = User Input + Explicit Config + Parent Config\n```\n\n**Priority Order:**\n1. User input from interactive prompts (highest priority)\n2. Explicit configuration from HCL\n3. Parent provider configuration (for child modules)\n\nThe `buildProviderConfig()` function handles this merging:\n\n```go\nfunc buildProviderConfig(ctx EvalContext, addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig,\n    config *configs.Provider) hcl.Body {\n    // Merge input and explicit config\n    // User input takes priority\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 Provider Plugin Architecture\n\nProviders are external plugins communicating via gRPC. The plugin lifecycle:\n\n1. **Discovery**: Providers found in `.terraform/plugins` or installed via provider requirements\n2. **Loading**: Plugin binary launched as subprocess\n3. **Handshake**: Protocol negotiation and capability discovery\n4. **Schema Fetch**: Request provider schema definition\n5. **Configuration**: Provider receives merged configuration\n6. **Resource Operations**: Provider executes Create/Read/Update/Delete operations\n7. **Cleanup**: Provider process terminates when `CloseProvider()` called\n\n### 2.4 Resource Operation Delegation\n\nWhen a resource operation is planned or applied:\n\n```\nNode.Execute()\n├── Get provider from EvalContext\n├── Request resource schema from provider\n├── Build request object (state + config)\n├── Call provider method (PlanResourceChange, ApplyResourceChange, etc.)\n├── Capture response (planned/new state, error)\n└── Update local state with response\n```\n\nEach provider method is responsible for:\n- Validating arguments\n- Computing differences (for Plan)\n- Making API calls\n- Handling errors\n- Returning updated resource state\n\n---\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### 3.1 State Structure\n\nThe `State` type represents Terraform's persistent state:\n\n```\nState\n├── Modules: map[string]*Module\n│   └── Module (for each module instance)\n│       ├── Resources: map[string]*Resource\n│       │   └── Resource\n│       │       └── Instances: map[addrs.InstanceKey]*ResourceInstance\n│       │           └── ResourceInstance\n│       │               ├── Current: *ResourceInstanceObject\n│       │               └── Deposed: map[DeposedKey]*ResourceInstanceObject\n│       └── Outputs: map[string]*OutputValue\n├── RootOutputValues: map[string]*OutputValue\n└── CheckResults: *CheckResults\n```\n\n**Key Properties:**\n- **Hierarchical**: Organized by modules and resources\n- **Instance-Based**: Resources can have multiple instances (count/for_each)\n- **Deposed Objects**: Tracks old objects during create-before-destroy operations\n- **Immutable Interface**: State should only be modified through `SyncState` methods\n\n### 3.2 State Synchronization (SyncState)\n\nFor concurrent graph execution, state is wrapped in `SyncState`:\n\n```go\ntype SyncState struct {\n    state    *State\n    writable bool\n    lock     sync.RWMutex  // Protects concurrent access\n}\n```\n\n**Features:**\n- Atomic operations: Multiple state changes happen together or not at all\n- Read-Write separation: Multiple readers or single writer\n- Deep copying: Returned values are independent copies\n- Automatic pruning: Empty modules are removed (except root)\n\n**High-Level Operations:**\n\n```go\n// Resource instance operations\nSetResourceInstanceCurrent(addr, obj, provider)\nDeposeResourceInstanceObject(addr) DeposedKey\nSetResourceInstanceDeposed(addr, key, obj, provider)\n\n// Output operations\nSetOutputValue(addr, value, sensitive)\nRemoveOutputValue(addr)\n\n// Module operations\nRemoveModule(addr)\n\n// Batch operations for planning\nUpdateResourceInstanceObjects(...)\n```\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Enables concurrent graph node execution without race conditions\n- Provides consistent snapshots for reading\n- Prevents partial state updates during failures\n\n### 3.3 Multiple State Versions During Execution\n\nTerraform maintains multiple state objects simultaneously during a walk:\n\n```\nState: Current state being built\n    ↑\n    └── Updated by Apply/Plan nodes\n\nRefreshState: State after refresh phase\n    ↑\n    └── Populated during refresh walk\n\nPrevRunState: State from previous run\n    ↑\n    └── Loaded at start, used for comparison\n```\n\n**Usage:**\n- `State`: Primary state being modified\n- `RefreshState`: Previous state snapshot (for change detection)\n- `PrevRunState`: Used for comparisons and understanding drift\n\nThis enables:\n- Change detection: Compare current vs previous state\n- Rollback capability: Previous state preserved\n- Consistency checking: Ensure applied changes match plan\n\n### 3.4 State Persistence and Backends\n\nState management is abstracted through the state manager interface in `statemgr` package:\n\n```\nBackend (e.g., S3, Azure Storage)\n    ↑\nState Manager (implements locking, versioning)\n    ↑\nLocal State File (JSON format)\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- **Reading**: Load state from backend\n- **Locking**: Prevent concurrent operations\n- **Versioning**: Track state history\n- **Persistence**: Write updated state back to backend\n\nThe Context holds a reference to the state manager for:\n- Initial state loading\n- Atomic write-back after successful apply\n- Lock management during operations\n\n---\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Hook System\n\n### 4.1 Overall Plan Execution Flow\n\n```\nContext.Plan(config, opts)\n│\n├─ 1. Build Plan Graph\n│   ├── PlanGraphBuilder.Build()\n│   ├── Apply transformers in sequence\n│   └── Return executable Graph\n│\n├─ 2. Refresh Walk (optional)\n│   ├── Walk graph with RefreshWalker\n│   ├── Call resource ReadState for current values\n│   ├── Update RefreshState with current values\n│   └── Returns refreshed state for comparison\n│\n├─ 3. Plan Walk\n│   ├── Walk graph with PlanWalker\n│   ├── For each resource node:\n│   │   ├── Call provider.PlanResourceChange()\n│   │   ├── Capture planned change (Create/Update/Delete/NoOp)\n│   │   └── Store in Changes\n│   └── Returns complete change set\n│\n└─ 4. Return Plan Object\n    └── Contains all changes ready for apply\n```\n\n### 4.2 Overall Apply Execution Flow\n\n```\nContext.Apply(plan, config, opts)\n│\n├─ 1. Build Apply Graph\n│   ├── ApplyGraphBuilder.Build(plan.Changes)\n│   ├── Only includes changed resources\n│   ├── Applies create-before-destroy ordering\n│   └── Return executable Graph\n│\n├─ 2. Apply Walk\n│   ├── Walk graph with ApplyWalker\n│   ├── For each resource change node:\n│   │   ├── Call provider resource operation (Create/Update/Delete)\n│   │   ├── Update state with result\n│   │   └── Call hooks (PreApply, PostApply)\n│   ├── Handle deposed objects cleanup\n│   └── Update State atomically\n│\n└─ 3. Return Updated State\n    └── State persisted to backend\n```\n\n### 4.3 Graph Traversal (Walker)\n\nThe DAG walker executes nodes respecting dependencies:\n\n```\nWalker Algorithm:\n│\n├─ For each vertex (node) in graph:\n│   ├── Wait for all dependencies to complete\n│   ├── If dependency failed: Skip or error (per graph semantics)\n│   ├── Execute node callback (concurrent if possible)\n│   ├── Collect diagnostics\n│   └── Mark vertex complete\n│\n└─ Return aggregated diagnostics from all vertices\n```\n\n**Key Walker Characteristics:**\n- **Parallel Execution**: Independent nodes execute concurrently\n- **Dependency Respect**: Nodes only execute after upstream dependencies complete\n- **Atomic Failures**: Failed nodes block downstream dependents\n- **Cancelable**: Graph walk can be stopped via context cancellation\n\n### 4.4 Execution in ContextGraphWalker\n\nThe `ContextGraphWalker` implements the Terraform-specific walker pattern:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    Context              *Context\n    State                *states.SyncState    // Main state\n    RefreshState         *states.SyncState    // Pre-walk state snapshot\n    Changes              *plans.ChangesSync   // Accumulates changes\n    Checks               *checks.State\n    NamedValues          *namedvals.State     // Variable/output tracking\n    InstanceExpander     *instances.Expander  // Count/for_each expansion\n    Operation            walkOperation\n    StopContext          context.Context\n}\n\n// Key method called for each node\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) Execute(ctx EvalContext, node GraphNodeExecutable) {\n    // Acquire parallelism semaphore\n    w.Context.parallelSem.Acquire()\n    defer w.Context.parallelSem.Release()\n\n    // Execute the node\n    return node.Execute(ctx, w.Operation)\n}\n```\n\n**Scope Management:**\n\nThe walker maintains multiple evaluation contexts, one per module:\n\n```go\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) enterScope(scope evalContextScope) EvalContext {\n    // Returns EvalContext scoped to a specific module\n    // Caches contexts to ensure consistency\n}\n```\n\nThis allows:\n- Module isolation\n- Variable scope containment\n- Provider configuration inheritance\n\n### 4.5 Hook System\n\nHooks are callback points allowing external code to observe and influence execution.\n\n#### Hook Interface\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    // Resource operation hooks\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        newState cty.Value, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Plan hooks\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        priorState, proposedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Provisioning hooks\n    PreProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, err error) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, line string)\n\n    // State refresh hooks\n    PreRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, newState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Import hooks\n    PreImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, importID string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []providers.ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Lifecycle hooks\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error)\n    Stopping()\n}\n```\n\n#### Hook Actions\n\n```go\ntype HookAction byte\n\nconst (\n    HookActionContinue  // Proceed normally\n    HookActionHalt      // Cancel operation\n)\n```\n\n#### Hook Execution Flow\n\n```\nFor each hook in Context.hooks:\n    Call hook method with resource details\n    ├─ HookActionContinue: Proceed to next hook\n    └─ HookActionHalt: Cancel operation, stop remaining hooks\n```\n\n#### Common Hook Uses\n\n1. **UI Output**: Display resource operations and status\n2. **Logging**: Track operations for audit\n3. **Monitoring**: Integrate with external systems\n4. **Validation**: Custom checks during apply\n5. **Deferral**: Implement custom pause/resume logic\n\n### 4.6 Dynamic Expansion During Execution\n\nCount and for_each resources are expanded dynamically during graph execution.\n\n#### Instance Expansion\n\n```\nInstance Expander tracks:\n├─ count.index / each.key / each.value for current iteration\n├─ length calculations for count\n├─ map iterations for for_each\n└─ Nested expansion for resource instances\n```\n\n**Expansion Process:**\n\n```\n1. InstanceExpander node executes\n   ├── Evaluates count or for_each expression\n   └── Creates abstract instances for each value\n\n2. Instance keys created: IntKey for count, StringKey for for_each\n\n3. Per-instance nodes created from abstract node\n   ├── NodeResourcePlanInstance\n   ├── NodeResourceApplyInstance\n   └── Can access instance key for self references\n\n4. Instances execute in graph order\n   └── Each instance has independent state/attributes\n```\n\n**Data Available to Instances:**\n\n```\nself.*              // Current resource's computed attributes\ncount.index         // Numeric index (count)\neach.key            // Map key (for_each)\neach.value          // Map value (for_each)\nresource.*.id       // Splat referencing other instances\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Evaluation Context\n\n### 5.1 EvalContext Interface\n\nThe `EvalContext` is the primary interface for node execution, providing access to:\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Module and path information\n    Path() addrs.ModuleInstance\n    Stopped() <-chan struct{}\n\n    // Provider operations\n    InitProvider(addr, config) providers.Interface\n    Provider(addr) providers.Interface\n    ProviderSchema(addr) providers.ProviderSchema\n    CloseProvider(addr) error\n    ConfigureProvider(addr, config) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n    // Provisioners\n    Provisioner(name) provisioners.Interface\n    ProvisionerSchema(name) *configschema.Block\n\n    // State and changes\n    State() *states.SyncState\n    RefreshState() *states.SyncState\n    Changes() *plans.ChangesSync\n    NamedValues() *namedvals.State\n\n    // Expression evaluation\n    EvaluateBlock(body, schema, self, key) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluateExpr(expr, wantType, self) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluationScope(self, source, key) *lang.Scope\n\n    // Hooks and plugins\n    Hook(callback func(Hook) error) error\n    Input() UIInput\n}\n```\n\n### 5.2 BuiltinEvalContext Implementation\n\nThe standard implementation provides:\n\n```go\ntype BuiltinEvalContext struct {\n    // Execution environment\n    StopContext  context.Context\n    InstanceExpander *instances.Expander\n\n    // Caches\n    ProviderCache      map[string]providers.Interface\n    ProvisionerCache   map[string]provisioners.Interface\n\n    // State and configuration\n    StateValue         *states.SyncState\n    ChangesValue       *plans.ChangesSync\n    ChecksValue        *checks.State\n    NamedValuesValue   *namedvals.State\n    DeferralsValue     *deferring.Deferred\n\n    // Configuration\n    ConfigValue        *configs.Config\n    PluginsValue       *contextPlugins\n\n    // Evaluation\n    EvaluatorValue     *Evaluator\n}\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains caches for provider/provisioner instances\n- Coordinates access to state and changes\n- Provides expression evaluation capabilities\n- Manages hook invocation\n\n### 5.3 Evaluation and Expression Handling\n\nThe `Evaluator` handles HCL expression evaluation:\n\n```\nExpression Evaluation:\n│\n├─ Parse expression as HCL\n├─ Build evaluation scope with:\n│   ├── Module variables\n│   ├── Local values\n│   ├── Resource references\n│   ├── Data source references\n│   └── Functions and operators\n├─ Execute evaluation in scope\n├─ Apply type conversion if needed\n└─ Return evaluated cty.Value\n```\n\n**Scope Includes:**\n- `self.*`: Current resource or data source\n- Variables from root and current module\n- Outputs from all modules\n- Data source read values\n- Locals from current module\n- References to other resources/data sources\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points\n\n### 6.1 Custom Transformers\n\nExtend graph building by implementing `GraphTransformer`:\n\n```go\ntype CustomTransformer struct {\n    // Configuration\n}\n\nfunc (t *CustomTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {\n    // Add, remove, or modify nodes and edges\n    return nil\n}\n\n// Register with graph builder\nbuilder.Steps = append(builder.Steps, &CustomTransformer{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Custom node scheduling\n- Integration-specific resource ordering\n- Cost optimization by graph reordering\n- Security enforcement via forced dependencies\n\n### 6.2 Custom Hooks\n\nImplement `Hook` interface to observe execution:\n\n```go\ntype CustomHook struct{\n}\n\nfunc (h *CustomHook) PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, ...) (HookAction, error) {\n    // Log, validate, or modify behavior\n    return HookActionContinue, nil\n}\n\n// Register with context\nopts.Hooks = append(opts.Hooks, &CustomHook{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Real-time operation monitoring\n- Cost estimation\n- Resource validation\n- Event forwarding to external systems\n- Custom approval workflows\n\n### 6.3 Provider Plugins\n\nProviders are the primary extension point. Implement the `providers.Interface`:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetSchema(ctx context.Context) (*ProviderSchema, error)\n    PrepareProviderConfig(ctx context.Context, req PrepareProviderConfigRequest) PrepareProviderConfigResponse\n    ValidateResourceConfig(ctx context.Context, req ValidateResourceConfigRequest) ValidateResourceConfigResponse\n    ReadResource(ctx context.Context, req ReadResourceRequest) ReadResourceResponse\n    PlanResourceChange(ctx context.Context, req PlanResourceChangeRequest) PlanResourceChangeResponse\n    ApplyResourceChange(ctx context.Context, req ApplyResourceChangeRequest) ApplyResourceChangeResponse\n    // ... more methods\n}\n```\n\n**Hook Points:**\n- Configuration validation\n- Resource diffing\n- Resource creation, update, deletion\n- State refresh\n- Data source reads\n\n### 6.4 Custom Provisioners\n\nImplement `provisioners.Interface` for post-apply provisioning:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetSchema(ctx context.Context) (*configschema.Block, error)\n    ProvisionResource(ctx context.Context, req ProvisionResourceRequest) ProvisionResourceResponse\n    Stop(ctx context.Context) error\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Configuration management (Ansible, Chef, Puppet)\n- Custom deployment scripts\n- Infrastructure validation\n- Service registration\n\n---\n\n## 7. Error Handling\n\n### 7.1 Error Propagation\n\nErrors are collected and propagated through the execution flow:\n\n```\nNode.Execute() returns tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    ↓\nDiagnostic collected in walker\n    ↓\nWalker stops dependent nodes\n    ↓\nAggregated diagnostics returned to caller\n```\n\n**Diagnostic Types:**\n- `Error`: Prevents operation and downstream nodes\n- `Warning`: Logged but doesn't block execution\n- `Detail`: Informational messages\n\n### 7.2 Failure Handling in Parallel Execution\n\nWhen a node fails:\n\n1. **Downstream Blocking**: Dependent nodes receive error signal and don't execute\n2. **Parallel Sibling Isolation**: Independent nodes continue executing\n3. **Partial Completion**: Some resources may have executed before failure\n4. **State Preservation**: State partially updated with successful operations\n\n**Recovery Strategy:**\n- User can fix error and rerun plan/apply\n- Partial state is not persisted without full success\n- Deferred resources allow deferring problematic resources to next run\n\n### 7.3 Non-Fatal Errors\n\nSome errors don't block execution:\n\n```go\ntype NonFatalError interface {\n    Diagnostics() tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\nThese allow:\n- Collection of multiple issues\n- User fixing issues in one pass\n- Proceeding with partial results when appropriate\n\n---\n\n## 8. Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\n┌─────────────────┐\n│  Configuration  │\n│   (HCL files)   │\n└────────┬────────┘\n         │\n         v\n┌─────────────────────────┐\n│  Config Loader          │\n│  (parses, validates)    │\n└────────┬────────────────┘\n         │\n         v\n┌─────────────────────────┐\n│ Graph Builder           │\n│ (PlanGraphBuilder)      │\n├─────────────────────────┤\n│ Steps:                  │\n│ 1. ConfigTransformer    │\n│ 2. ExpandTransformer    │\n│ 3. ReferenceTransformer │\n│ 4. ProviderTransformer  │\n│ 5. ... (more)           │\n└────────┬────────────────┘\n         │\n         v\n    ┌─Graph─────┐\n    │ Nodes     │\n    │ (abstract)│\n    │ Edges     │\n    │ (deps)    │\n    └─────┬─────┘\n          │\n          v\n┌──────────────────────────────┐\n│ Concrete Node Conversion      │\n│ (factories apply)             │\n└──────────┬───────────────────┘\n           │\n           v\n     ┌─Graph────────┐\n     │ Executable   │\n     │ Nodes        │\n     │ (concrete)   │\n     │ Edges        │\n     └──────┬───────┘\n            │\n            v\n   ┌────────────────────┐\n   │ Refresh Walk       │ ← (optional)\n   ├────────────────────┤\n   │ ContextGraphWalker │\n   │ RefreshState       │\n   │ (ReadResource ops) │\n   └────────┬───────────┘\n            │\n            v\n   ┌────────────────────┐\n   │ Plan Walk          │\n   ├────────────────────┤\n   │ ContextGraphWalker │\n   │ Changes (build)    │\n   │ Hooks: Pre/Post*   │\n   └────────┬───────────┘\n            │\n            v\n    ┌───Plan Object───┐\n    │ Changes         │\n    │ ResourceChanges │\n    │ OutputChanges   │\n    └────────┬────────┘\n             │\n             v\n   ┌──────────────────────────┐\n   │ Graph Builder            │\n   │ (ApplyGraphBuilder)      │\n   │ (rebuilds from plan)     │\n   └───────────┬──────────────┘\n               │\n               v\n         ┌─Graph─────┐\n         │ Apply Ops │\n         └─────┬─────┘\n               │\n               v\n    ┌──────────────────────┐\n    │ Apply Walk           │\n    ├──────────────────────┤\n    │ ContextGraphWalker   │\n    │ State (update)       │\n    │ Hooks: Pre/Post*     │\n    │ Provider operations  │\n    └──────────┬───────────┘\n               │\n               v\n      ┌───Updated State────┐\n      │ Resources          │\n      │ (new attributes)   │\n      │ Outputs (computed) │\n      └────────┬───────────┘\n               │\n               v\n    ┌──────────────────┐\n    │ Backend Persist  │\n    │ (state file)     │\n    └──────────────────┘\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Performance Considerations\n\n### 9.1 Parallelism\n\nGraph execution naturally parallelizes:\n\n**Without Dependencies**: 100 independent resources execute concurrently (up to parallelism limit)\n\n**With Dependencies**: Resources execute in dependency order, but siblings execute in parallel\n\n```\nExample:\naws_vpc.main (Parallelism: 1/10)\n├─ aws_subnet.a (Parallelism: 2/10)\n├─ aws_subnet.b (Parallelism: 3/10)\n└─ aws_subnet.c (Parallelism: 4/10)\n   ├─ aws_instance.1 (Parallelism: 5/10)\n   ├─ aws_instance.2 (Parallelism: 6/10)\n   └─ aws_instance.3 (Parallelism: 7/10)\n```\n\n### 9.2 State Access Optimization\n\n`SyncState` minimizes lock contention:\n\n- Atomic operations reduce lock time\n- Deep copies prevent concurrent mutations\n- Module-level granularity allows targeting\n- Read-write separation maximizes parallelism\n\n### 9.3 Graph Construction Time\n\nLarge graphs (100s of resources) build in milliseconds:\n\n- Transformers run sequentially (single-threaded)\n- Most transformers run in O(n) or O(n log n)\n- TransitiveReduction can be expensive (O(VE)) but optional\n\n### 9.4 Execution Time Optimization Opportunities\n\n1. **Targeted apply**: Only resources with changes\n2. **Parallelism tuning**: `-parallelism=N` flag\n3. **Resource ordering**: Explicit `depends_on` for critical paths\n4. **Deferred actions**: Postpone problematic resources\n5. **Caching**: Provider schemas cached, reused across module instances\n\n---\n\n## 10. Key Architectural Patterns\n\n### 10.1 Builder Pattern\n\nThe `BasicGraphBuilder` + `GraphTransformer` chain:\n\n```\nEmpty Graph → Step 1 → Step 2 → ... → Step N → Final Graph\n```\n\nEach step is independent, composable, and testable.\n\n### 10.2 Visitor Pattern\n\n`GraphWalker` visits each node and executes it:\n\n```go\ntype GraphWalker interface {\n    Execute(EvalContext, GraphNodeExecutable)\n}\n```\n\nAllows flexible execution strategies (sequential, parallel, with caching, etc.)\n\n### 10.3 Strategy Pattern\n\nOperation-specific behavior through factories:\n\n```go\n// Plan operation\nconcretePlan := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodePlanResourceInstance{...}\n}\n\n// Apply operation\nconcreteApply := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodeApplyResourceInstance{...}\n}\n```\n\n### 10.4 Template Method Pattern\n\nAbstract nodes define the template, concrete nodes implement steps:\n\n```go\ntype NodeAbstractResourceInstance struct {\n    // Common attributes\n    Addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\n    // Implemented by concrete nodes\n    Execute() // Defined in NodePlanResourceInstance, etc.\n}\n```\n\n### 10.5 Observer Pattern\n\nHooks observe execution:\n\n```go\nHook interface {\n    PreApply(...)\n    PostApply(...)\n    // ... other observation points\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform's plan/apply architecture is built on these key principles:\n\n1. **Graph-Based Execution**: Dependencies drive parallelism\n2. **Phase Separation**: Planning and application are distinct phases\n3. **Plugin Architecture**: Providers implement resource operations\n4. **Thread-Safe State**: SyncState enables concurrent execution\n5. **Extensible Design**: Transformers and hooks allow customization\n6. **Composable Components**: Each piece is testable and replaceable\n7. **Error Isolation**: Failures don't corrupt state\n8. **Transparent Execution**: Hooks enable observation and control\n\nThis architecture enables Terraform to handle complex infrastructure as code scenarios with reliability, performance, and extensibility.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
